~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


You may download and print this FAQ, but under no circumstances can you
put this FAQ on your web page without our permission.  You MAY NOT ALTER
IT IN ANY WAY or claim it as your own.

From this point on, I will only be sending FAQ updates to GameFAQs, IGN,
and Tekken Zaibatsu.  Anyone who has recevived permission to host any of
the Tekkenomics FAQs also has permission to host any of our future
text-based FAQs (unless specified), and can obtain updates from any of
the previously mentioned websites.




~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
~                                                                        ~
~                           3. FAQ Description                           ~
~                                                                        ~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


Shortly after the release of Tekken: Dark Resurrection (TDR) for the
PlayStation Portable (PSP) in July 2006, I was in the process of
updating all of my Tekken 5 (T5) FAQs for TDR.  But, halfway through the
process, my harddrive crashed, and I lost all of my data.  I was going to
give up on trying to update the FAQs for TDR, but I got an idea.  Since
TDR is essentially an upgrade of T5, my idea was to use my T5 FAQs as a
reference and only write one FAQ that covers things that are unique to TDR.
This FAQ covers new moves, changed properties, hidden moves, combos,
customizations, taunts, secrets, and a few other things.  Because of this,
I will also periodically update my T5 FAQs.  Feel free to contribute
anything to any of my FAQs.


Because TDR is an upgrade to T5, most of the commands for T5 are the same
for TDR, and most of the combos still work.  However, there are some changes
in TDR that affect these two categories.  I will try to point out those
differnces with this FAQ, as well as add new material that is specific to
TDR.


This FAQ covers the U.S. versions of Tekken: Dark Resurrection for the PSP
and Tekken 5: Dark Resurrection for the PS3.  The things in this FAQ should
work in the Arcade and other PSP/PS3 versions of T5DR, but they were only
tested with the U.S. version.


The "Character Strategy & Combos" Forums at Tekken Zaibatsu is also a
great place to find strategies and combos for your favorite fighter:
http://www.tekkenzaibatsu.com/forums/forumdisplay.php?forumid=102




~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
~                                                                        ~
~                                4. Legend                               ~
~                                                                        ~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


This is a list of the notations that I will be using throughout this FAQ.
This Legend is very similar to the one used by Tekken Zaibatsu, however
there are a few differences.


RECENT CHANGES: FLM to FLA, MNP to MNT, KNDW to KNDA, PNX to AOP
NEW ADIITIONS: DKI, HPF, LBR, LCT, LWV, MST, NEG, RDP, RWV, WND


-----------------------------
          Buttons
-----------------------------


 Notation     Meaning
 --------     -------

  1           Left Punch (Square)
  2           Right Punch (Triangle)
  3           Left Kick (X)
  4           Right Kick (Circle)


-----------------------------
         Direction
-----------------------------


 Notation     Meaning
 --------     -------

  f           Press Forward (Towards opponent)
  F           Hold Forward (Towards opponent)
  F#          Hold Forward until next D-Pad command
  b           Press Backward (Away from opponent)
  B           Hold Backward (Away from opponent)
  B#          Hold Back until next D-Pad command
  u           Press Up
  U           Hold Up
  U#          Hold Up until next D-Pad command
  d           Press Down
  D           Hold Down
  D#          Hold Down until next D-Pad command
  D/B#        Hold Down/Back until next D-Pad command
  D/F#        Hold Down/Forward until next D-Pad command
  qcb         Quarter Circle Backward; Down to Back (d,d/b,b)
  QCB         Quarter Circle Backward; Down to Back (d,d/b,B)
  qcf         Quarter Circle Forward; Down to Forward (d,d/f,f)
  QCF         Quarter Circle Forward; Down to Forward (d,d/f,F)
  hcf         Half Circle Forward (b,d/b,d,d/f,f)
  HCF         Half Circle Forward (b,d/b,d,d/f,F)


NOTE1: D-pad represents the arrows (up, down, left, right) on the
       PS2 controller or Arcade stick

NOTE2: "F#" requires you to hold forward for a longer period of time
       than "F".


-----------------------------
       FAQ Notations
-----------------------------


 Notation     Meaning
 --------     -------

  #           Hold; Hold indicated button(s) until that move is executed
                 or until N (Neutral)
  ( _ )       Or; Choose one of the moves within the parenthesis to do
  ~           Press button immediately after
  /           Press indicated directional buttons at the same time
  +           Press buttons at same exact time
  N           Leave joy pad neutral
  *           Short pause between button presses
  **          Medium pause between button presses
  ***         Long pause between button presses
  [ ]         Optional command(s)
  { }         Action within these must be completed in order for the command
                 to be executed correctly
  :           The command following this requires "just frame" input
  ( )...      Repeat the pattern within the brackets
  ,           Separates commands
  <           Delayed input
  =           Next in sequence


-----------------------------
      Action Notation
-----------------------------


 Notation     Meaning
 --------     -------

  BLK         Attack must be blocked by opponent
  BT          Back Towards Opponent
  cd          Crouch Dash (f,N,d,d/f)
  CD          Crouch Dash (f,N,d,D/F)
  CH          During Counter Hit/Attack
  CL          Clean Hit
  ecd         Electric Crouch Dash (f~N,d~d/f)
  FC          Full Crouch; While Crouching
  GRAB        Opponent must be grabbed from the front
  HIT         While opponent is being hit (damaged)
  HIT*        After opponent is hit (damaged)
  OBT         Opponent's Back Turned
  OCR         Crouching Opponent
  OGR         Grounded Opponent (Opponent on ground)
  Parry       Move is parried
  RevL        While opponent is reversing your left attack
  RevR        While opponent is reversing your right attack
  SS          Side Step
  SSL         Side Step Left
  SSR         Side Step Right
  SSW         Side Step Walk
  TAC         Tackle
  WR          While your fighter is running; While running
  WS          While standing from a crouch; While Rising


-----------------------------
     Grounded Positions
-----------------------------


 Notation     Meaning
 --------     -------

  FDFA        Face down & feet away
  FDFT        Face down & feet towards
  FUFA        Face up & feet away
  FUFT        Face up & feet towards
  GRND        While lying on ground
  KNDA        Right after the opponent knocks to you the floor


NOTE: You might see the following alternative notations used:
  FDFA = SLD (Slide position)
  FDFT = FCD (Face Down position)
  FUFA = PLD (Play Dead position)
  FUFT = KND (Knockdown position)

NOTE: You might see the following alternative notations used:
  AOP = PNX (Phoenix) - Lei Wulong or Ling Xiaoyu
  FLE = POG (Pogo Stance) - Yoshimitsu
  RLX = NEG (Negativa) - Christie Monteiro / Eddy Gordo
  SDW = LBR (Labyrinth) - Raven
  VTS = RDP (Ready Position) - Craig Marduk
  WND = CES (Clockwise Evasive Spin) - Julia Chang


-----------------------------
    Combo Specific Legend
-----------------------------


These are commands that relate to the combo section.


All combos will be written in the format:
 move; move; ... (damage)


 Notation     Meaning
 --------     -------

  {}          The stance that you should be in after executing the
                previous move
  ( )         For the combo to work, this move will not hit the
                opponent
  [+/- dmg]   The amount of damage that the launcher adds to or
                subtracts from the total
  ;           Separates different moves used within a combo
  *           Possibility of escape from full damage
  WALL        Your opponent must hit a wall
  WGF         Wind Godfist (f,N,d,d/f+2)
  EWGF        Electric Wind Godfist (f~N,d~d/f+2)
  DEWGF       Dashing Electric Wind Godfist
  WHF         Wind Hookfist (f,N,d,d/f+2)
  EWHF        Electric Wind Hookfist (f~N,d~d/f+2)
  DEWHF       Dashing Electric Wind Hookfist
  ecd         Electric Crouch Dash (f~N,d~d/f)
  BIG         Combos that will only work on large opponents
  CC          Crouch Cancel
  iWS         Instant While Standing




~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
~                                                                        ~
~                         5. Legend Explanations                         ~
~                                                                        ~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


1)  + -> and

    Christie Monteiro
      Rasteila to Handstand
           d/b+3, B

      Press "d/b" and "3" at the same exact time.


2)  [ ] -> Optional command
   
    Bryan Fury
      Vulcan Cannon Body Blow
          D/F#+1, 1, [1], [1], 2

      This move can be expanded into these moves...
         Vulcan Cannon Body Blow 1
              D/F#+1, 1, 2
         Vulcan Cannon Body Blow 2
              D/F#+1, 1, 1, 2
         Vulcan Cannon Body Blow 3
              D/F#+1, 1, 1, 1, 2


3)  ( _ ) -> or

    Steve Fox
      Left Right Left to Swaying
           1, 2, 1, b+(3 _ 4)

      This move can be performed by doing:
         1, 2, 1, b+3
      or by doing...
         1, 2, 1, b+4
      Only one of these commands is needed.


4)  "Dragon Fake Step to Dragon Sign Stance" Explanation

    Marshall Law
      Dragon Fake Step to Dragon Sign Stance
           DCT ~ b, f, f

    Explanation: Performing a move that can be transitioned into DFS by
    pressing "b,f" afterwards can be transitioned into DSS by pressing
    "b,f,f" instead.

    An example can be shown with the Junkyard Kick:
    In this example, "b+2,3,4" is the DCT move.
    Junkyard Kick to Dragon Fake Step
         b+2, 3, 4 ~ b, f
    Junkyard Kick to Dragon Sign Stance
         b+2, 3, 4 ~ b, f, f


5)  "Dragon Sign Stance Transition" (DSST) Explanation

    Explanation: Performing a move that can be transitioned into DSS by
    pressing "b,f" afterwards, such as 1,2~b,f.


6)  "Indian Stance Motion Taunt" (Explanation)
    Yoshimitsu
      Indian Stance Motion Taunt
           INS, 3+4#, (1 _ 2 _ 1+2), (u _ d _ f _ b)
    While in Yoshimitsu's Indian stance, hold down "3+4".  While
    still holding these buttons, press "1" or "2".  Then while you are
    still holding down "3+4", press any directional D-PAD button.
    You will hear Yoshimitsu's taunt whenever you press any D-PAD
    button.
   
    NOTE1: During this entire hidden move, you will be holding down the
           "3+4" buttons.

    NOTE2: Pressing the "1", "2", or "1+2" buttons will give you three
           different taunts.


7)  AOP,BT (Explanation)

    Ling Xiaoyu
      Reverse Phoenix Mistrust
           AOP, BT, 4

    "AOP,BT" means that you are in the AOP stance with your back
    towards your enemy.  This can occur when you are in "AOP"
    and the opponent jumps over you or sidesteps around you.


8)  Crouched Step Combo (Explanation)
      FC, d/f, d, d/f, N, f+(Any button preceded by f,f)

    For example, Lee has the following "Crouched Step Combo" moves:
    Crouched Step to Pulse Blast
         FC, d/f, d, d/f, N, f+3
    Crouched Step to Deadly Edge
         FC, d/f, d, d/f, N, f+4

    However, this move doesn't seem to work with Lee's f,f+3+4 grab.


9)  Snakeshot Rolling Dash Punch Combo (Explanation)
      SS+1, F, 1, (Any move preceded by d/f+1)

    For example, Nina has the following moves:
    Snakeshot Rolling Dash to 10-Hit Combo 2
         SS+1, F, 1, 2, 1, 2, 3, 3, 2, 1, 2, 4
    Snakeshot Rolling Dash to Double Explosion 3
         SS+1, F, 1, 2, F+1+2
    Snakeshot Rolling Dash to Spider Knee Combo
         SS+1, F, 1, 2, 3


10) Soul Omen (Explanation)

    Jin Kazama - Soul Omen
         b+1+2#, d, u, b, f

    "Soul Omen" is performed from Jin's "Power Stance" (b+1+2).
    During the execution of the move you will hold "1+2" until you see Jin
    perform "Mental Alertness" (Check out Jin's in-game move list to see
    what it looks like).  You are able to input the "d,u,b,f" part quickly
    or at normal speed.  The most important part is to make sure that you
    are still holding "1+2".

    Right after you execute Jin's soul omen, you have a window of 5
    seconds to perform any Soul Omen with the letters "SOM" in front of it
    (See "Hidden Moves" section).

~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
~                                                                        ~
~                             7. Definitions                             ~
~                                                                        ~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


- "Clean Hit" and "Juggle" definitions taken from the "Still Standing"
  website (http://www.manji-clan.com/wtcl/index.html)
- "okizeme" and "Tech roll" definition by sithlord
- For more words, check out "The Tekken Zaibatsu Jargon Dictionary":
  http://www.tekkenzaibatsu.com/forums/showthread.php?threadid=92806


Clean Hit
    Hitting your opponent from very close range.  Clean hits inflict
    more damage than a normal hit.  However, not all attacks will be
    able to become a clean hit.


Counter Hit
    Occurs when you hit an opponent that is getting ready to attack
    or is in the process of attacking.  Counter hits inflict more
    damage than a normal hit.


Ground roll
    To roll around while lying down on the ground (not instantly after
    hitting the ground like "tech roll").


Juggle
    An event that occurs when a character is thrusted into the air by an
    attack followed by a series of combos, punches or kicks while falling
    down to the ground. The juggling process stops once the character has
    hit the ground.


Launcher
    A move that makes it possible for your opponent to be juggled.
    (Also known as "Juggle Starter")


Okizeme (often called "oki")
    Japanese for "wake-up". In other words, the art of hitting someone on
    the ground or as they try to get up.


Tech roll
    To instantly roll away and then stand up the moment your body impacts
    the ground.


Whiff
    An attack that does not touch the opponent.  The attack misses the
    opponent completely.

~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
~                                                                        ~
~                       9. Changed Move Properties                       ~
~                                                                        ~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


In this section, you will find a list of move properties that have
changed from Tekken 5 (for PS2).



-------------------------------------------------------------------
                           Anna Williams
-------------------------------------------------------------------


- d/f+1,2,3 (Uppercut Jab to Radiant Arch)
Flips the opponent over in the air puts them in FDFA position
instead of launching them.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
                           Bryan Fury
-------------------------------------------------------------------


- f+3 (Knee Strike)
Now stuns on a counter hit.

- b+1 (Chopping Elbow)
Now launches on CH only.

- WS+3 (Kigh Knee Kick)
On counter hit, opponent will now be in an inescapable stun.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
                             Feng Wei
-------------------------------------------------------------------


- 2~1 (Pummeling Windmill)
On hit, puts opponent into crouching position instead of FDFA position.

- u+4 (Right Vertical Jump Kick Launcher)
No longer launches on normal hit.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
                              Ganryu
-------------------------------------------------------------------


- WS+1+2 (Rising Hammer)
On hit, lifts the opponent straight up into the air instead of
making them flip in the air.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
                          Kazuya Mishima
-------------------------------------------------------------------


- WS+2 (Demon God Fist)
On hit, opponent will be in an inescapable stun.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
                           Lei Wulong
-------------------------------------------------------------------


- 3~4,u,u (Tornado Kicks)
On hit, puts opponent in crouching position instead of knocking them
back into FUFT position.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
                          Ling Xiaoyu
-------------------------------------------------------------------


- d/f+2~1 (Cross Lifting Palms)
On launch, the opponent will launch normally instead of flipping
over like in Tekken 5.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
                         Nina Williams
-------------------------------------------------------------------


U/F+4 (Leaping Axe Kick)
No longer hits grounded opponents.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
                         Paul Phoenix
-------------------------------------------------------------------


- b+3 (Lights Out)
Now has crumple fall property on normal hit instead of crumple stun
on counter hit.

- f+2,3 (Quick PK Combo)
Opponent will be in a crumple stun if only second hit connects on a
counter hit.

- SS+1 (Turn Thruster)
Opponent will be in a crumple stun on a counter hit.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
                              Raven
-------------------------------------------------------------------


- f+4 (Lance Kick)
Knocks the opponent straight back and down to the ground instead of
floating slightly to the right.

- u+3,3 (Deathbringer Mid)
Changed hit properties from m,h to h,h

- u+3,d+3 (Deathbringer Low)
Changed hit properties from m,L to h,L

- u+3,4 (Deathbringer High)
Changed hit properties from m,h to h,h

- b+2,2,3 (Unicorn's Tail)
Now only launchers on when the the third hit connects on a counter hit.
On normal hit, the third hit now makes the opponent flip over into the
FDFA position.

- b,b+2 (War Hound)
Now knocks the opponent down into the FUFA position on normal hit.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
                           Steve Fox
-------------------------------------------------------------------


- d/f+2 (Right Uppercut)
Now launches on CH only.

- f+3,f,2 (Power Skyscraper)
Launches a lot higher now.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
                           Wang Jinrei
-------------------------------------------------------------------


- d/b+1 (Cobra Fang)
On counter hit, opponent enters a crumple stun and falls forward instead
of entering an escapable stun and falling backwards.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
                           Yoshimitsu
-------------------------------------------------------------------


- 4~3 (Kangaroo Kick)
Opponent is now launched further out instead of straight up into the air.
The same applies for "u/f+3+4,3+4", "3,d+3+4", "INS,4" and "INS,3,3+4".

- f+3+4 (Kamikaze)
On hit, both Yoshimitsu and the opponent will be knocked to the ground
into the FUFT position.  Transition into Indian Stance is no longer
possible.  When used in a combo, Yoshimitsu will remain standing after
the move connects.

- D/B+1+2#,(3_4) (Back Stomach to Backflip Kick)
Now launches on counter hit when the opponent is behind you.

- b,b+1,1+2 (Face Splitter)
Now stuns the opponent on counter hit.

- DGF,3 (Dragonfly Sweep)
No longer trips the opponent on normal hit.

~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
~                                                                        ~
~                             11. Combo List                             ~
~                                                                        ~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


In this section, you will find a list of combos using the new TDR moves,
changed move properties, and combos that are only available in TDR.  Check
out my "Tekken 5 Combo FAQ" for more combos.  Be aware that some T5 combos
no longer work in TDR, however that information will not be covered in
this FAQ.

Tekken 5 Combo FAQ
http://www.gamefaqs.com/console/ps2/file/920588/37553

NOTE1: For most launchers, the guaranteed damage total doesn't begin until
       the opponent is launched.  Not all of the hits are guaranteed to hit
       the opponent, so the actual damage may be less in the combo listed
       below.  The damage after each combo below assumes that the opponent
       isn't blocking during the combo (unless indicated).  It was easier
       for me to write it this way.

NOTE2: Some juggle starters from Tekken 5 that begin by knocking the
       opponent to the ground are no longer guaranteed in T5DR, as the
       opponent can now perform a backroll.

For more combos, check out the "Character Strategy & Combos" sections on
Tekken Zaibatsu forums:

Tekken 5 Character Strategy & Combos
http://www.tekkenzaibatsu.com/forums/forumdisplay.php?forumid=61

Tekken 5: Dark Resurrection Character Strategy & Combos
http://www.tekkenzaibatsu.com/forums/forumdisplay.php?forumid=102

~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
~                                                                        ~
~                         13. Customization Items                        ~
~                                                                        ~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


Here is a list of the buyable customization items and colors available
within Tekken: Dark Resurrection.

An item that is available for a fighter's Punch AND Kick costumes only
need to be purchased once, then it will be available to equip for both
costumes.

NOTE: The customization items do not affect the fighter's abilities.

* = New item/color added for Dark Resurrection
** = Changed from Tekken 5 (PS2)



-------------------------------------------------------------------
                          Aura Information
-------------------------------------------------------------------

Within Dark Resurrection, every fighter has Aura available to them
which can only be equipped with custom colors.  Equipping Aura will
remove equipped items from every part of the body.  Equipping Auras are
handled differently in the PSP and PS3/Arcade versions.



=======================================
     PSP Version
=======================================

Within the PSP version:
- Every fighter has the same Aura colors and levels available for
  purchase.
- The Auras are available under the "Aura" menu when customizing your
  fighter.
- At the beginning, you only have one Aura color and level available,
  but more can be unlocked by winning matches within the Tekken Dojo mode.
- Purchasing an Aura for one fighter makes it available for every other
  fighter as well.

The Auras available are:

Tempest Aura (Lv. 1) - 1,000 G (White)
Tempest Aura (Lv. 2) - 1,000 G
Tempest Aura (Lv. 3) - 1,000 G
Tempest Aura (Lv. 4) - 1,000 G

Life Aura (Lv. 1) - 1,000 G (Green)
Life Aura (Lv. 2) - 1,000 G
Life Aura (Lv. 3) - 1,000 G
Life Aura (Lv. 4) - 1,000 G

Burning Aura (Lv. 1) - 1,000 G (Pink)
Burning Aura (Lv. 2) - 1,000 G
Burning Aura (Lv. 3) - 1,000 G
Burning Aura (Lv. 4) - 1,000 G

Raging Aura (Lv. 1) - 1,000 G (Red)
Raging Aura (Lv. 2) - 1,000 G
Raging Aura (Lv. 3) - 1,000 G
Raging Aura (Lv. 4) - 1,000 G

Dark Aura (Lv. 1) - 1,000 G (Purple)
Dark Aura (Lv. 2) - 1,000 G
Dark Aura (Lv. 3) - 1,000 G
Dark Aura (Lv. 4) - 1,000 G

Arctic Aura (Lv. 1) - 1,000 G (Blue)
Arctic Aura (Lv. 2) - 1,000 G
Arctic Aura (Lv. 3) - 1,000 G
Arctic Aura (Lv. 4) - 1,000 G

Golden Aura (Lv. 1) - 1,000 G (Yellow)
Golden Aura (Lv. 2) - 1,000 G
Golden Aura (Lv. 3) - 1,000 G
Golden Aura (Lv. 4) - 1,000 G



=======================================
     PS3 / Arcade Versions
=======================================

Within the PS3 and Arcade versions:
- The Aura is available under "Lower Body" when customizing your
  fighter and sells for 20,000 G.
- "Random Aura Change" is only selectable after Aura has been purchased,
  and only randomly changes you aura level and color.  This sells for
  30,000 G.  You will have to spend 30,000 G every time you wish to
  change your aura color or level.  Also, purchasing "Random Aura Change"
  appears to only apply to one of the fighter's costumes.
- In the PS3 and Arcade versions, aura level and color cannot be selected.
- Unlike the PSP version, purchasing an Aura for a fighter only makes it
  available for both of that fighter's costumes.

~                                                                        ~
~              14. Dark Resurrection Default Costume Colors              ~
~                                                                        ~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


Tekken 5: Dark Resurrection changes the colors of the default costumes
that were used in Tekken 5.  This section lists the colors used for the

~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
~                                                                        ~
~                               17. Taunts                               ~
~                                                                        ~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


The following is a list of pre-match and post-match taunts that are
available within Dark Resurrection that aren't available in Tekken 5.
Check out my "Tekken 5 Taunts FAQ" for information on the other taunts.

Tekken 5 Taunts FAQ
http://www.gamefaqs.com/console/ps2/file/920588/37580



-----------------------------------------------------------
                         Legend
-----------------------------------------------------------

To perform one of the indicated indicated taunts, hold one or a
combination of the face buttons (square, triangle, X, O) buttons.

For a "Post-Match Taunt", being holding the button after winning the
final round of a match, during the match replay.  To speed things up,
you can press the "Start" button while holding down one of the face
buttons.

There is currently no way to select a "Pre-Match" taunt.


1: Press Left Punch button (Square)
2: Press Right Punch button (Triangle)
3: Press Left Kick button (X)
4: Press Right Punch button (Circle)
1+2: Press both punch buttons at same time
3+4: Press both kick buttons at same time
?: The button combination to get this taunt is unknown.  The only known
   way to get this taunt is for it to appear randomly by not pressing
   any buttons.
U: Press "up" on the controller


There is an explanation for each taunt.  If there is a better explanation
for a taunt, please let me know, and you will receive credit for your
contribution.



-----------------------------------------------------------
                     Pre-Match Taunts
-----------------------------------------------------------

Armor King
?: Gets up from ground with back turned, then turns around.
?: Crosses arm over chest twice, then goes into fighting stance.
?: Performs the "Capital Punishment" (u/f+1+2).
?: Does the crab stretch, but uses head instead of arms.


Bryan Fury
?: Raises left knee, raises left arm half-way, then leans back.


Jinpachi Mishima
?: Puts arms in air, then spreads them apart while laughing.


Lee Chaolan
?: Does a spinning kick, spins, then ends in the Hitman Stance.


Lili (Emily Rochefort)
?: Puts hand on chin and says "How long can you stand my attacks."
?: Laughs while looking down, then turns and says "You surely don't
   belive... you can beat me."
?: Does a side flip , then a back flip, throws hands back.
?: Looks down then turns while saying "My battles... are for my
   father."
?: Walks up and says "This is a great place to fight, don't you think?"
   while flicking hair.


Raven
?: Walks toward the opponent, vanishes then re-appears being the
   opponent.


Sergei Dragunov
?: Looks at hand while making a fist, then looks towards the camera.
?: Walks up, then strokes side of face with two fingers.


Steve Fox
?: Throws weak right-left punches, bumps fists together, then
   turns head towards camera.


Wang Jinrei
?: Sits on the ground with head lowered and eyes closed, then
   looks up.



-----------------------------------------------------------
                    Post-Match Taunts
-----------------------------------------------------------

Armor King
1: Points at camera, then gives two thumbs down.
2: Does the cut-throat taunt then gives one thumb down.
3: Looks up towards the sky.
4: Shrugs then growls.


Baek Doo San
?: Does two double high kicks.


Devil Jin
4: Force choke.


Ganryu
1+2: Runs, then does a sumo splash on grounded opponent.


Heihachi Mishima
?: Laughs while swinging arms around, then says "That felt good. Next!".


Jinpachi Mishima
1: Opens arms and lets out a growl.
2: Holds out right hand and says "Die!"
3: SAME AS #1
4: SAME AS #2


Julia Chang
?: Puts hands on chest, takes a deep breath, bows, then gives a
   thumbs up.


Kazuya Mishima
?: Does the "Hell Lancer" (cd+3), then the "Glorious Demon God
   Fist" (f+1+2).


Lili (Emily Rochefort)
1: Walks towards camera, makes the quiet sign and says "Please don't
   tell my father".
2: Has hands clasped together while looking down, then looks up and
   spreads arms and says "The moment of victory... I love it!"
3: Walks past downed opponent, then says "Sebastian, they say they're
   leaving already."
4: Puts left on hip, lets out a sigh, then says "Sebastian, can't you do
   better than this?"
1+2: Says "It's time for my afternoon tea. Farewell." and does a curtsee.
3+4: Does a twisting flip, front flip, then lands in a kneeling position.


Nina Williams
?: Turns over grounded opponent with her foot then looks at them.


Paul Phoenix
1+2: Kneels down near grounded opponent, taps a 1,2,3 count, then
     gets up and cheers.
3+4: Attempts a somersault, but fails and lands face down.


Roger Jr.
?: Stands on tail, spins around, then puts both arms in the air.


Sergei Dragunov
1: Strokes cheek while looking at the camera, then walks away.
2: Dusts off clothes with hand, looks at camera, then walks away.
3: Brushes side of face with two fingers while looking at the camera,
   then walks away.
4: SAME AS #2



-----------------------------------------------------------
                      Other Taunts
-----------------------------------------------------------

When you lose a match, your fighter will do one of several losing poses if
you are in a mode with a continue screen.  The following is a list of the
ones that I have seen are:

- Falls on butt.
- Walks forward, puts hands up, then turns around.
- Drops to one knee and holds head while looking at the ground.
- Shrugs, then turns away.
- Falls to ground sideways.
- Falls to knees and throws a small tantrum.




~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
~                                                                        ~
~           18. Secrets / Unlockables / Nice-To-Know (TDR/PSP)           ~
~                                                                        ~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


The following information is from a thread on Tekken Zaibatsu, created
by Jaytech, titled "Tekken DR PSP Secrets/Unlockables/Nice-To-Know"
http://www.tekkenzaibatsu.com/forums/showthread.php?threadid=94308

Contribution: Jaytech, Wild Man X, Drake the Demon, Koston, Esseph,
              MYK [jamgi], Keviiinn, James Pham, H.K. Lei, tae-kwon-do


This is for all the stuff that you can unlock (how/when?) in DR on the
PSP.  This is a good way to get an overview of the game's features.


-----------------------------------------------------------

GENERAL:


- The start+select feature is still working, which is the command for
  in-game reset.
- For the first costume of each character press "1" or "2", and for
  the second one press "3" or "4" (this applies to nearly all chars;
  Kuma and Panda: 1_2 and 3_4, respectively).
  All special outfits are unlocked right from the start and are
  selectable by pressing "2" and in special cases also with "4" (Asuka
  and Ling).  Ling's schhol girl outfit is selected with the "R" button.
- Changing of the main menu wallpaper:
  (It appears that you get the wallpapers according to the amount of
  Tekken Lords you have)
  This is the order in which you get them:
  Kazuya's Hand (default), Jin's Hand (1 TL), Devil Jin's Hand (3 TL),
  Jinpachi and random (5 TL)
- The game runs at 60fps on the PSP (this excludes the fmvs and the
  character intros before each fight, which run at 30fps).
- Required space for the savegame on the Memory Stick is 128KB. An
  additional 3.25MB is needed for ghosts of your fighters (~65KB each).
- The savegame ONLY works with the PSP you created it on (the reason
  seems to be the online ranking feature.)
- Version changes: The Japanese version of the game has a graphical
  glitch (a white square appears in place of sparks).  The U.S. version
  seems to be fixed (happens rarely, mostly after the game has been set
  to sleep-mode).  The European version has been fixed completely, and
  in stage 0, you only fight characters between the ranks of lord of war
  and divine fist.  If you put the PSP in sleep mode during a fight, no
  white squares will appear; the game doesn't freeze after you turn on
  the psp; custom connections don't work on the EU game; the aura
  unlockables can be unlocked by beating 9 players in arcade battle.


-----------------------------------------------------------

STORY MODE:


- Beat story-mode once for theatre mode
- Beat story-mode twice for command attack
- Beat story-mode 3 times for tekken bowling, time attack and gold rush
- Completing story-mode earns you 100,000g for each character's
  individual playthrough (only once per character) and you get the
  prologue and epilogue movies in theatre mode (note: Kuma and Panda
  have separate storylines/movies).


-----------------------------------------------------------

THEATRE MODE:


- Jinpachi's Final Transformation Vid is available after you lose to
  Jinpachi and do not continue (same as in tekken 5 for ps2), or you
  can just purchase it in theatre mode.
- Character prologue/epilogue movies are unlocked by beating story mode
  with each individual character.
- Additional movies:
  2006 E3 trailer - beat command attack 5 times around 1min 30sec
  Tekken 5 Opening Movie Console Part 1 - beat Time Attack (finish it,
       final time doesn't matter)
  Opening Movie Console Part 2 - earn more than 5000G in one round in
       Gold Rush
  Tekken Dark Resurrection Opening Movie (AC Version) - beat Survival
       Mode (become #1 on the record list)


-----------------------------------------------------------

ARCADE MODE:


- Final rank in arcade mode is "Dark Lord" (a.k.a. Tekken Lord Black).
  You can fight against "Divine Fist" (a.k.a. Fist god) characters, but
  won't get that ranking there (see "Tekken Dojo" below for more info).
- Different auras/aura levels are unlocked by getting up ranks in arcade
  mode.
- Tekken roulette has more variations now (x2,x3,x5,x10 and x5,x10)
- Ranking up follows the same procedure as in Tekken 5: promotion after
  winning about 5-7 consecutive times against same (+/- 2 ranks) ranked
  opponents, demotion after losing about 5 consecutive times (note: when
  using the start+select feature, the next time you play arcade mode you
  start where you left off.  This means you that you can get a promotion
  or demotion match as your first match.)
- After you rank up to "divine fist" for the first time in Tekken Dojo
  stage 6, you can then earn the rank in arcade mode as well.

- Arcade Mode Ranking:

Beginner (brown)
9th - 1st Kyu (dark red)
1st - 7th Dan (grey)
Shihan (grey)
Expert (grey)
Warrior (grey)
Master (grey)
Virtuoso (grey)
Champion (grey)
Lone Wolf (green)
Destroyer (green)
Berserker (green)
Sage (green)
Legend (green)
Fujin (blue)
Raijin (blue)
Deity (blue)
Lord of War (blue)
Dragon Lord (yellow/orange)
Tekkenlord (yellow/orange)
Dark Lord (black/orange; final rank in arcade mode)
Divine Fist (white/red; ultimate special rank/obtainable in Tekken Dojo
     the first time/thereafter also obtainable in arcade mode; see below)


-----------------------------------------------------------

TEKKEN DOJO (TD):


- Dojos: Stage 1 (Earth Dojo), Stage 2 (Water Dojo), Stage 3 (Fire Dojo),
         Stage 4 (Wind Dojo), Stage 5 (Void Dojo), Stage 6 (Heaven Dojo),
         Stage 0 (Yurin Dojo)
- You can earn free items/colors/auras/aura levels by completing stages
  in Tekken Dojo (you must not purchase them earlier).  You will be
  re-imbursed for any item or color that you purchase beforhand.
- After finishing stage 3 you get the chance to fight Jinpachi. After
  winning, Stage 0 and Stage 4 are unlocked.
- After finishing Stage 5 you get the chance to fight Jinpachi. After
  winning, you unlock Jinpachi's ghost, Stage 6, 300,000g for clearing
  and an additional 3,000,000g (only first time you ever beat it).
  If you lose to Jinpachi in stage 3/5, your dojo ranking in this stage
  will stay at #2 until you beat him, and you can't proceed to the next
  dojo.
- After finishing Stage 6 you get 300,000g for clearing and the special
  ranking "Divine Fist" (a.k.a. "Fist God") if you are on "Dark Lord"
  (a.k.a. "Tekken Lord Black") when beating the survival tournament.
  (NOTE: This only works if Tekken Dojo difficulty is set to normal)
  (Also, you CAN get demoted after reaching the "Divine Fist" rank)
- While playing through Tekken Dojo, you unlock TD Time Attack (Water
  Dojo), TD Survival (Fire Dojo), TD Gold Rush (Wind Dojo), and TD
  Roulette Battle (Void Dojo). After unlocking new modes, they also
  become available in earlier stages (excluding Roulette Battle).


-----------------------------------------------------------

TEKKEN BOWL:


--------------------
Radar-Vision Bowlers
--------------------

The following bowlers have a special radar-vision:
Bryan Fury, Jack-5, Yoshimitsu


------------
Bowling hand
------------

Left Handed Bowlers
Anna Williams, Lee Chaolan, Lili, Steve Fox

Ambidextrous Bowlers (press "select" to switch hands)
Baek Doo San (Left default), Hwoarang (Right default),
Kuma/Panda (Right default)

Everyone else is a right-handed bowler.


--------------
Bowling speeds
--------------

Extremely Fast Bowlers (Max speed above 80 km/h)
Ganryu, Jack-5

Very Fast Bowlers (Max speed of 70-80 km/h)
Armor King, Bryan Fury, Craig Marduk, Eddy Gordo, Kuma/Panda,
Paul Phoenix, Sergei Dragunov

Slow Bowlers (Max speed of 40-45 km/h)
Christie Monteiro, Nina Williams

Very Slow Bowlers (Max speed of 40 km/h and below)
Anna Williams, Asuka Kazama, Lili, Ling Xiaoyu

Extremely Slow Bowlers (Max speed less than 30 km/h)
Roger Jr., Wang Jinrei

Everyone else is about average (45-70 km/h)


----------------
Additional Notes
----------------

- Within "Striker" mode, you get an extra ball for every 5 consecutive
  strikes.
- Pressing left or right before releasing the ball will make the ball
  go a little bit more in that direction.
- The following things will make your bowler fly towards the bowling
  pins, but will count as a foul:
     - Timeout = Don't press anything for one minute.
     - Overcharge = Get the power bar at its absolute maximum.
- Bowling style:
     In tekken bowling during the shiftment of your character left
     and right, press square once and then bowl as usual to see a
     unique bowl. Press square again at the shiftment of your character
     to turn it off.

MULTIPLAYER:


- The game features Wi-Fi compatibility (ad-hoc) and infrastructure
  (upload and download content only).
- ALL different region versions (JPN/US/EUR) of the game are compatible
  with each other, however it seems there is more lag between different
  versions.
- Gamesharing doesn't allow stage select, needs time to download content
  before each fight, doesn't support custom control settings for player 2
  and has less lag than UMD/UMD multiplayer.

PLAYSTATION STORE


- What is Tekken 5: Dark Resurrection?
"Tekken 5: Dark Resurrection" is an arcade-perfect port, which
means that it was designed to be like the arcade version of the
game.  This also means that it doesn't have the extra modes
available in the PSP version.

- Where can I purchase Tekken 5: Dark Resurrection?
T5DR can be purchased on the PlayStation Store for $19.99 US.
To access T5DR after logging into the store, navigate to:
Games > PS3 Games > Tekken 5: Dark Resurrection (Full Game)

GENERAL

  and 3_4 respectively). All special outfits are unlocked right from
  the start and are selectable via 2 and in special cases also with 4.

-----------------------------------------------------------

VERSUS BATTLE


- You can copy your saved data and send it to the other profiles on
  your machine. So, if you and a buddy want different customizations,
  he can simply unlock gold on a separate ID on your PS3, and send his
  save over to your ID before you play and you'll both be able to pick
  your own costumes. However, the game still will not keep track of
  wins & loses, nor can you unlock gold like this.

I also noticed that I was able to copy the save file to my flash drive.
So, in theory you should be able to simply copy your save onto a usb
storage medium, go to a buddy's house, and just copy your data to his
profile and use your personal customizations that way as well or send
your file to someone over the computer and they can transer it to their
PS3.

NOTE: This is no longer possible when the save file is converted to
      T5DR Online.


-----------------------------------------------------------

GAMEPLAY


- It seems that obtaining gold is much more straight forward than in
  the PSP counterpart... you play the game... you get gold, easy enough...

- So far I have seen the gold peak at around 15,000G per match (that is
  not including roulette)

- No indication of the Divine Fist rating being a part of this game.
  However, it was brought to my attention that the loading sign is
  that of the Divine Fist... so there may be a possibility...

- I achieved a Dark Lord status with Devil Jin and lo and behold...
  nothing happened...

- Within Ghost Mode, it keeps track of how much gold you have obtained
  during your current run. However, it doesn't add in if you receive a
  roulette multiplier on it. Also, if you lose to the computer, you
  lose your "streak" of gold and must restart from 0.

Seems as if the game was meant to be a true arcade port... with not much
else added....


-----------------------------------------------------------

GLITCHES/OTHER STUFF OF INTEREST


- The Secret Garden (Night) - for one reason or another, there seems
  to be a problem on this stage. It is only cosmetic wise and will
  not affect gameplay. However, it looks weird as the "sparks" that
  occur during a move just dont happen. Devil Jin for example will
  throw out an EWGF and there wlll be no electricity on his hands.
  This happens with a lot of moves...

- Ominous Mist - Not so much a glitch, but the resolution on this
  stage is drastically reduced from the other stages. Not really
  sure why though.

- The Secret Garden (Day) - Same thing as the Ominous Mist... it
  just doesn't look as pretty as the rest of the game...


-----------------------------------------------------------

TECHNOLOGY


For those of you who have played the game, you may notice that there
is a bit of lag between the inputs on the controller and the action
on the screen. I had it too. Although I was not able to fully fix the
problem without the addition of third party adapters, here is some
interesting info.

If you are running a TV on 1080i there may be a lag. Hate to say it,
but its true. So far there are a range of reports from a small amount
of lag during the grab animation that doesn't affect the gameplay at
all to there being a constant delay on everything, and that isn't good.

I personally pushed my TV down to 760p after experiencing this and the
lag was reduced, although it was not gone. But you probably will be able
to adapt. After a few minutes of working, all of Steve's flicker combos
were coming out fine and I was able to hit Hwoarang's JFSR 99% of the
time. Playing at 1080p is reported to work fine, being that it is the
resolution that the game was intended to be played on.

Playing with the sixaxis controller is also something that takes some
getting used to. The Diagonals aren't as giving as the dualshocks were,
so there might be a little frustration there. There is also the issue
with the controller having to re-sync with the PS3. This causes a
momentary inability to move your character. Last night I played on a
streak of around 500 matches... it happened to me like three times...
so it isn't bad, just something that needs to be considered for
tournament play.

Also... I dont know how the adapters are working for people...

T5DR ONLINE Q & A <UPDATE>

-----------------------------------------------------------

PLAYSTATION STORE


- What is Tekken 5: Dark Resurrection Online?
"Tekken 5: Dark Resurrection Online" is an expansion to
"Tekken 5: Dark Resurrection" for the PS3 which adds an online
multipayer mode, and the standard practice and survial modes.


- Where can I purchase Tekken 5: Dark Resurrection Online?
T5DRO can be purchased on the PlayStation Store for $9.99 US.
To access T5DRO after logging into the store, navigate to:
Add-Ons > Downloadable Game Add-Ons > Tekken 5: Dark Resurrection Add-On >
Tekken 5: Dark Resurrection Online Expansion (Add-On Content)

Alternatively, you can get them both at the same time by purchasing the
bundle for $29.99.  To access T5DRO bundle after logging into the store,
navigate to:
Games > Bundles > Tekken 5: Dark Resurrection Online Bundle (Full Game
and Add-On)

NOTE: If you previously purchased T5DR or T5DR Online seperately, you
      will not be able to download the bundle.


- How do you re-download T5DR/Online
If for some reason you need to re-download T5DR/Online, follow these steps:
     1. Log into the PlayStation Store under the account you used to
        purchase T5DR/Online.
     2. In the upper right hand corner of the screen, click on the "View
        Downloads" icon.
     3. Scroll down until you locate T5DR/Online.
     4. Click on T5DR/Online to begin download.


- What are the download sizes?
T5DR (only) = 555 MB
T5DR Online (only) = 591 MB
T5DR Online Bundle = ? (at least 591 MB)

MODES


(Informaion taken from the T5DRO Online Manual; URL located above)

Arcade Battle
     - "In this mode, you try to win a series of battles against
        the computer. After selecting a character and starting the
        game, the first match begins. If you defeat all opponents,
        you will have cleared the Arcade Battle Mode."

Ghost Battle
     - "In this mode, ghost opponents appear one after another.
        The difficulty level you set in Game Options under Options
        will apply only to the first opponent.  After that, the
        difficulty will very depending on the opponent you select
        to fight. Ghosts will continue to appear until you lose a
        match [or choose to exit]."

VS Battle
     - "This mode is exclusively for challenging another player
        to a battle. Customize Data may be used to battle another
        playing using a customized character."

Online Battle (T5DRO only)
     - "Battle other players over the PLAYSTATION Network. Refer
        to in-game instructions for details regarding controls or
        game play."

Survival (T5DRO only)
     - "Defeat a series of opponents with limited health."

Practice (T5DRO only)
     - "Select a character, an opponent character, and a stage,
        to practice various techniques in this mode."

Gallery (More images added)
     - "In this mode, you can purchase and enjoy movies and other
        content with the fight money you've earned."

Options
     - "Configure game options, sound options, controller setup
        or delete save data here."

~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
~                                                                        ~
~                         21. Earning Money (PSP)                        ~
~                                                                        ~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


This section lists several ways to earn money within Tekken: Dark
Resurrection for the PSP.


NOTE: For all battles where money is earned based on ranks, you will earn
      more money for a win when reaching the higher ranks.

      For example, a Tekken Lord defating a Tekken Lord will earn 4000G
      instead of 2000G for some modes.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
-                          Quick Battle                           -
-------------------------------------------------------------------


==============================
     VS CPU <NEW>
==============================


For this mode, it looks like you earn the same amount of money for each
win, but the amount of money earned increases with the difficulty setting.
The number of rounds fought doesn't seem to affect the money you earn,
so to earn money quicker, set the number of rounds to 1 under "Options".

Some of the amounts earn for different difficulty settings are below:
Easy - 2500G
Medium - 3000G
Ultra Hard - 5500G



==============================
     Team Battle <NEW>
==============================


For this mode, it looks like you earn the same amount of money for each
win, but the amount of money earned increases with the difficulty setting.
Also, you will receieve a boonus only if you win the Team Battle.

Some of the amounts earn for different difficulty settings are below:
Easy - 500G for each match won + 3000G for each win
                                    (only if you win the Team Battle)
Medium - 1000G for each match won + 3000G for each win
                                       (only if you win the Team Battle)
Ultra Hard - 2500G for each match won + 4000G for each win
                                           (only if you win the Team Battle)



-------------------------------------------------------------------
-                       Story Battle <NEW>                        -
-------------------------------------------------------------------


For this mode, it looks like you earn the same amount of money for each
win, but the amount of money earned increases with the difficulty setting.
The number of rounds fought doesn't seem to affect the money you earn,
so to earn money quicker, set the number of rounds to 1 under "Options".

Some of the amounts earn for different difficulty settings are below:
Easy - 2500 for each win
Ultra Hard - 5500G for each win



-------------------------------------------------------------------
-                       Arcade Battle <NEW>                       -
-------------------------------------------------------------------


For this mode, you earn money based on the difference between your
opponent's rank and yours.  This is what I have seen so far:

Opponent with a lower rank = 2000G
Opponent with same rank = 3000G
Opponent with higher rank = 3000G + (200 X # of ranks higer than you)

The number of rounds set doesn't appear to affect the amount of money
earned, so it is recommended to set matches to only 1 round.

The difficulty setting for this mode only affects the ranking of your
first opponent.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
-                          Network <NEW>                          -
-------------------------------------------------------------------


I'm not sure, but I'm guessing the amount of money earned in this mode
is similar to the single-player modes.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
-                           Tekken Dojo                           -
-------------------------------------------------------------------


NOTE: All of the modes listed below are not available for every dojo.


==============================
     League Match <NEW>
==============================


For Normal difficulty, you can earn the following amount of money for a win:
Opponent with a lower rank = 1000 G
Opponent with same rank = 1500 G
Opponent with higher rank = 1500 G + (100 G X # of ranks higher than you)

When you finish all matches in the league, you will earn a bonus based
on your final ranking.



==============================
     Survival Tournament <NEW>
==============================


For Normal difficulty, you can earn the following amount of money for a win:
Opponent with a lower rank = 1000 G
Opponent with same rank = 1500 G
Opponent with higher rank = 1500 G + (100 G X # of ranks higher than you)

When you finish all matches in the league, you will earn a bonus based
on your final ranking.



==============================
     Ranking Tournament <NEW>
==============================


For Normal difficulty, you can earn the following amount of money for a win:
Opponent with a lower rank = 1000 G
Opponent with same rank = 1500 G
Opponent with higher rank = 1500 G + (100 G X # of ranks higher than you)

When you finish all matches in the league, you will earn a bonus based
on your final ranking.



==============================
     Free Battle <NEW>
==============================


For Normal difficulty, you can earn the following amount of money for a win:
Opponent with a lower rank = 2000 G
Opponent with same rank = 3000 G
Opponent with higher rank = 3000 G + (200 X # of ranks higher than you)



==============================
     Challenge Battle <NEW>
==============================


- Time Attack

Similar to the other modes, you will earn money based on the difference
between the ranks of you and your opponent.  You will only receive a bonus
if you defeat all opponents within the given time limit.


- Survival

Similar to the other modes, you will earn money based on the difference
between the ranks of you and your opponent.  You will only receive a bonus
if you defeat all opponents with a limited amount of health.


- Gold Rush

For this mode, you earn money based on the amount of damage inflicted
on the opponent, and you lose money based on the amount of damage you
take.  You will only receive a bonus if you defeat survive the time limit
and obtain the pre-defined amount of fight money within the time limit.


- Roulette Battle

For this mode, it looks like you will earn 100G for each win, but this
amount will get multiplied by a random multiplier (I've seen 2x to 100x).
After 2 matches, you will get a chance to quit and keep all the money
you've earned or continue and risk losing 3/4 of your earnings.  You
have a limited amount of health.  You will only receive a bonus if you
earn the predefined amount of fight money.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
-                             Attack                              -
-------------------------------------------------------------------


==============================
     Time Attack <NEW>
==============================


For this mode, you will play a series of 9 matches and will earn
3000G for each match won.

After completing all 9 stages, you will earn 27000G plus a Bonus
based on your final time.

The number of rounds and difficulty cannot be changed for this mode.



==============================
     Survival
==============================


Fight against a series of never ending enemies where your health
increases a small amount after each victory.

Below, for each win within the ranges on the left will get you the
Reward on the right:
  1-3: 2500
  4-6: 3000
  7-9: 3500
10-14: 4000
15-19: 4500
20-24: 5000
25-29: 5500
30-34: 6000
35-39: 6500
40-44: 7000
45-49: 7500
50-??: 8000

Money earned = Reward (from each win) + Bonus (1000G X # of wins)

Difficulty level and number of rounds have no affect in this mode.



==============================
     Gold Rush <NEW>
==============================

For this mode, you earn money based on the amount of damage inflicted
on the opponent, and you lose money based on the amount of damage you
take.  It looks as if you earn more money for higher difficulty
settings.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
-                           Bonus Games                           -
-------------------------------------------------------------------


==============================
     Tekken Bowl <NEW>
==============================


- 1 Player
For this mode, tt looks as if your final score is based on your
final score, number of strikes, and number of spares.  I'm not quite
sure what the final breakdown is.


- 2 Player
I haven't played this mode recently, but I'm guessing the amount of
money earned is similar to the "1 Player" mode.


- Tournament
I haven't played this mode recently, but I'm guessing the amount of
money earned is similar to the "1 Player" mode.


- Striker
For this mode, I have seen the following:
Reward = (Final score X 100) + Bonuses earned from strikes

You earn an extra ball for every 5 consecutive strikes.

The bonus earned increases by 100 for each consecutive strike and you
will earn a 1500G bonus for the 5th consecutive strike.



==============================
     Command Attack
==============================


For this mode, you will need to perform a combination of commands
and combos chosen at randon (total of 10).  To go on to the next
command every hit must touch the opponent.

Money earned = Reward (based on final time) + Bonus (see below)

More informatin about the "Bonus":
- Bonus for each move is earned by completing commands consecutively.
  You can make a mistake and still earn the bonus, as long as you don't
  touch the opponent when you make the mistake.
- For each consecutive move, the bonus earned increases by 50G.
- You earn an additional "Perfect" bonus of 1000G when making no mistakes.
- For the bonus, the amount of time spent for each move isn't important.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
-                  Extra: Earn Free Items <NEW>                   -
-------------------------------------------------------------------


By defeating Ranking Tournaments within the Tekken Dojo mode, you will
unlock free items or colors for your character.  You will re-imbursed
for any item or color that you purchase beforhand.

To unlock the Auras, play the Tekken Dojo and Arcade modes.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
-                  Extra: Tekken Roulette <NEW>                   -
-------------------------------------------------------------------


Within several modes, you have a chance to get something known as
"Tekken Roulette".  After a win, you might get a chance to multiply your
winnings for that match by 2, 3, 5, or 10.  You will know that you're
going to get a roulette if you see a red flashing light above your life
bar.  "Tekken Roulette" appears randomly and may appear consecutively.

~                                                                        ~
~                         22. Earning Money (PS3)                        ~
~                                                                        ~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


This section lists several ways to earn money within Tekken 5: Dark
Resurrection Online for the PS3.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
-                          Arcade Battle                          -
-------------------------------------------------------------------


"Arcade Battle" is similar to the standard "Time Attack" mode, where you
face against 9 opponents.

You earn the following amount for money per win for every match:
Easy = 2500G
Medium = 3000G
Hard = 3500G
Very Hard = 4000G
Ultra Hard = 5000G

The number of rounds set don't affect on the amount of money earned,
so it is recommended to set matches to only 1 round.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
-                          Ghost Battle                           -
-------------------------------------------------------------------


You can earn several bonuses from those mode, with the total earned
equaling:
Win Bonus + Life Bonus + Time Bonus + Special Bonus

I've had a hard time predicting the amount of money earned for the
"Win Bonus", so here is my guess:
Opponent with a lower rank = 1500G
Opponent with same rank = 3000G
Opponent with higher rank = 3000G-4600G (estimate)

The number of rounds set doesn't appear to affect the amount of money
earned, so it is recommended to set matches to only 1 round.

The difficulty setting for this mode only affects the ranking of your
first opponent.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
-                            VS Battle                            -
-------------------------------------------------------------------


It isn't possible to earn money from Versus Battle.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
-                          Online Battle                          -
-------------------------------------------------------------------


I haven't spent very much time in Online Battle, so the numbers below
are just some estimated I have seen.

The total amount earned is from Win Bonus + Special Bonus.  

For a loss, you should earn a Win Bonus of 0G and Special Bonus of 500G.

For a win, majoirty of the time I have seen a Win Bonus of 2000G, but
in one instance I have seen a Win Bonus of 3500G.  I'm not sure how
the Special Bonus is calculated for a win, but I have seen 900G-2100G.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
-                            Survival                             -
-------------------------------------------------------------------


Fight against a series of never ending enemies where your health
increases a small amount after each victory.

You can earn several bonuses from those mode, with the total earned
equaling:
Win Bonus + Life Bonus + Time Bonus + Special Bonus

Below, for each win within the ranges on the left will get you the
Win Bonus on the right:
  1-5: 2500G
 6-10: 3000G
11-15: 3500G
16-??: 4000G

Difficulty level and number of rounds have no affect in this mode.



-------------------------------------------------------------------
-                  Extra: Tekken Roulette <NEW>                   -
-------------------------------------------------------------------


Within several modes, you have a chance to get something known as
"Tekken Roulette".  After a win, you might get a chance to multiply your
winnings for that match by 2, 3, 5, or 10.  You will know that you're
going to get a roulette if you see a red flashing light above your life
bar.  "Tekken Roulette" appears randomly and may appear consecutively.

=======================================
     Downloading YouTube Videos
=======================================


YouTube does not allow you to directly download videos from their website,
however there are a few workarounds to make downloading videos possible.


One solution is to use a website that reads in a YouTube URL and converts
the file online, then returns you a link to the converted file for
download.  To find these types of sites, you can google "youtube video
converter".

One site that I have successfully used is:
Online FLV Converter (http://vixy.net)


If you use the Mozilla FireFox web browser, you have another solution
available to you.  You can download the "Video DownloadHelper" add-on,
which allows you to download a YouTube video in the FLV format, or
convert it to several other formats with the use of an additional
desktop application.  More information is available below:

Firefox Add-on - Video DownloadHelper
https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/3006


If you chose to download the video in the FLV format and are having
issues playing the file with Windows Media Player or another media player,
you can try one of the following media players:

VLC Media Player (http://www.videolan.org/vlc/)
FLV Player (http://download.cnet.com/FLV-Player/3000-13632_4-10467081.html)

~                                                                        ~
~                              25. Questions                             ~
~                                                                        ~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


In this section, I will try my best to answer questions that I have
received through e-mail.


----------
Question 1 - DEWGF and WDEWGF
----------

Q: How do you do DEWGF and WDEWGF?

A: I'm not good at doing DEWGF or WDEWGF, but this link might help:
   http://www.tekkenzaibatsu.com/forums/showthread.php?threadid=87686


----------
Question 2 - Long time between updates
----------

Q: What took so long for another update to come out?

A: I was working on an update soon after I released the last version.  At
   the time, I was storing the file that I was updating only on a portable
   hard drive that I got from Best Buy about two months earlier.  One day,
   that hard drive decided to stop working and I was unable to retrieve
   the file I was working on.  I was so angry about losing all of the work
   that I put into the update I was working on that I decided to stop
   updating the FAQ.  However, I recenetly received some questions about
   T5DR, which re-kindled my interest in updating the FAQ again.  A word
   of caution: DON'T BUY THE WESTERN DIGITAL PASSPORT POTABLE HARDDRIVE!


----------
Question 3 - Customize on PSP
----------

Q: How do I get to the character customization on the PSP version?

A: In the "Mode Select" menu, go to "Profile" > "Customize".


----------
Question 4 - Customize on PS3
----------

Q: How do I get to the character customization on the PS3 version?

A: While at the character select screen before a match begin, after
   selecting a fighter, you will see a small menu appear on the upper
   portion of the screen.  In this menu, highlight and select
   "ITEM SHOP & EQUIP" to get to the customization items.  Within this
   menu, you can also change the name your profile name.


----------
Question 5 - Unequipping items
----------

Q:  How can I unequip an item?

A:  To unequip an item on the PSP, you will have to highlight the
    equipped item (box that is colored blue), press the "X" button,
    then select "Yes" when it asks you to unequip the item.

    The different box colors are:
    Red = item has not yet been purchased
    Blue = item is currently equipped
    Green = item has been purchased, but is not currently equipped
    
    To unequip an item on the PS3, while in the "ITEM SHOP & EQUIP" menu,
    select the "NO EQUIP" box.


----------
Question 6 - Convention Ranking
----------

Q:  What does "Convention Ranking" mean (for the PSP version)?

A:  It is the ranking system for your continent.


----------
Question 7 - PS3 Vibration
----------

Q: How do you turn off the vibration for PS3 when playing DR?

A: To turn off the vibration, you can either do it from the XMB before
   or within the game.

   To do it before the game has been loaded:
   - Go to Settings > Accessory Settings
   - Scroll down to "Controller Vibration Function", then set to "Off".

   To do it after the game has been loaded:
   - Hold down the "PS" button in the middle of the controller until you
     see a black screen with four menu options in the center.
   - Go down to "Controller Settings"
   - Click on "Vibration Function" and set it to "Off"

   You'll have to go through one of the above options again to turn the
   vibration back on. T5DR doesn't have a setting to turn off the
   vibration within the game itself.


----------
Question 8 - T5DR Frame Data
----------

Q: Do you know where I can find frame data for T5DR?

A: You can find T5DR frame data, as well as a guide that explains how to
   use it SD Tekken: http://sdtekken.com/t5dr/frame-data/


----------
Question 9 - Colored Square Boxes
----------

Q: Next to the ghost's name and rank, what do the different colored square
   boxes mean?

A: They stand for the differnt continents:
Red = Asia
Green = North America
Blue = Europe
Pink = South America
Orange = Africa
Light Blue = Oceania (Australia)


-----------
Question 10 - Setting PSP Wallpaper
-----------

Q: How can I set wallpaper on the PSP?

A: To set the wallpaper:
- In the XMB (or the PSP's home menu), navigate to the "Photo" section,
  and click on the :Memory Stick" icon.
- Select an image that you like and view it by selecting it with the "X"
  button.
- While the image is displayed, press the "Triangle" button, then
  select "Set as Wallpaper".
- Select "Yes" when prompted.


-----------
Question 11 - Setting PS3 Wallpaper
-----------

Q: How can I set wallpaper on the PS3?

A: To set the wallpaper:
- In the XMB (or the PS3's home menu), navigate to the "Photo" section.
- Select an image that you like and view it by selecting it with the "X"
  button.
- While the image is displayed, press the "Triangle" button, then
  select "Set as Wallpaper".
- Here a white box surround the image.  Everything within the box will be
  selected to display as the wallpaper.  Use the left analog stick to move
  the box horizontal or verticle and the right analog stick to zoom in or
  out.  When done, press the "X" button and select "Yes" when prompted.


-----------
Question 12 - Breaking Throws
-----------

Q: Do you have any tips for breaking throws?

A: I'm not an expert on breaking throws, but "Rip" of Tekken Zaibatsu has
   created a "Throw Break Trainer" that might help:
   http://tekken.reepal.com/index.php/tbt/


-----------
Question 13 - Online Battle Character Icon
-----------

Q: For the PS3 version, how do I select the character icon shown under my
   profile in "Online Battle"?

A: There doesn't appear to be any way to select the which character icon
   is used.  It looks like the way that it decides which character to use
   is that it selects whichever character is #1 under "Character Usage".


-----------
Question 14 - Game Save Backup?
-----------

Q: Is it possible to backup your game save data for Dark Resurrection on
   the PSP and PS3?

A: For the PSP, it is possible to backup your data, but the save data will
   only work with the PSP the save was created on.

   For the PS3, you are able to backup your save data for Dark Resurrection
   and even transfer to different PS3 accounts, but this is not possible with
   Dark Resurrection Online.

~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
~                                                                        ~
~                          27. About Tekkenomics                         ~
~                                                                        ~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


The main purpose of "Tekkenomics" is to provide you with Tekken FAQs/Guides
and to keep you updated on Tekken news and information.

"Tekkenomics" was originally the name of the website created by me
(Wild Man X), with help from Paulinstein and Drake the Demon, which first
came online on November 6, 2004.  However, due to someone engaging in
piracy on our hosting server the website went down in April 2007.  With
the release of Tekken 6 approaching for consoles, I decided to bring back
Tekkenomics, but in the form of a blog back in June 2009.

"Tekkenomics" contains various Tekken related material, some of which is
difficult to find on any other Tekken based website.  The blog will
contain exclusive articles, original FAQ files, move lists, combos/juggles,
combo videos, in-game matches, Tekken commercials, PC desktop wallpaper,
PSP wallpaper, CG art, fan-based material, and other things.

If you're having problems visiting the "Tekkenomics Blog" at
http://www.tekkenomics.com, then you can also visit it at the following
link: http://tekkenomics.wordpress.com

If you were wondering how we came up with the name "Tekkenomics", back in
my high school days in the year 2000, Paulinstein, me, and some other high
school friends would get together to play Tekken 3 on the PlayStation 1.
At the time, we were also enrolled in Economics. Whenever we would get
together to play, we would say that we were going to study some
"Tekkenomics".  So, basically: "Tekken" + "Economics" = "Tekkenomics".

There are a few references on the web to the name "Tekkenomics" that
aren't related to us or our blog.  There are some members on the Tekken
Zaibatsu forums that go by the names "Tekkenomics", "Tekkenomics_101",
and "TekkenNomics Jr." that aren't related to us. On Tekken Zaibatsu,
we go by the names "Wild Man X", "Paulinstein", and "Drake the Demon".
The things on the web that ARE related to us are at: GameFAQs, Neoseeker,
IGN, 1UP.com, Gamerhelp, Gamespot, MySpace, AIM, MSN Messenger, Hotmail,
GMail, YouTube, PicasaWeb, Blogger, WordPress, ImageShack, and Twitter.

~                          28. About the Author                          ~
~                                                                        ~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


I have been a fan of the Tekken series since 2000.  A few of my friends
got me into the series with Tekken 3.

My first FAQ was "Hidden Moves" for Tekken 4.  Writing this FAQ, I've
learned some new things about Tekken along the way that I probably
wouldn't have learned otherwise.  My FAQs are a way for me to share
what I have learned.

Lei Wulong is my main fighter, and has been since Tekken 3.  When I bought
Tekken Tag Tournament for the PS2, I decided to learn how to play with all
of the fighters, and this has carried over to Tekken 4, Tekken 5, and
Tekken: Dark Resurrection.  So, you can rest assured that I do atleast
know a little bit about what I'm talking about :)

I am currently residing in Southern California (in the United States),
but have not been to any of the arcades in the area in a long time.  I
used to play at the University of California, Riverside.

I hope that you've enjoyed my FAQs!
